This causes an infinite restart loop and interrupts active tasks. (Affects `src/cli/gateway-cli/run-loop.ts` and `src/daemon/systemd-unit.ts`)\\n- **Root Cause**: The generated systemd unit uses `KillMode=control-group`. In some environments, when a CLI process is launched from a terminal within the same user session, it inherits the Gateway service\\u0026#39;s cgroup. When the CLI process exits, systemd\\u0026#39;s state management or session teardown can propagate a spurious `SIGTERM` to the entire cgroup, terminating the Gateway. Furthermore, the Gateway immediately shuts down upon receiving `SIGTERM` even if it just started.\\n- **Fix**: \\n  i. Changed systemd `KillMode` from `control-group` to `mixed`. This ensures systemd only sends `SIGTERM` to the main Gateway process on an intentional unit stop, while residual children still receive `SIGKILL` after `TimeoutStopSec`. This prevents CLI processes from propagating signals to the Gateway.\\n  ii. Added a `serverStarting` guard in `run-loop.ts`. If a `SIGTERM` is received precisely during the `params.start()` execution window, it is logged as a warning and ignored. This acts as a robust defense mechanism against the rapid restart loops, while ensuring that `SIGTERM` is always honoured once the server is listening or if it fails to start.\\n- **What changed**: \\n  - `src/daemon/systemd-unit.ts`: Changed `KillMode=control-group` to `KillMode=mixed`.\\n  - `src/daemon/systemd-unit.test.ts`: Updated tests to assert `KillMode=mixed`.\\n  - `src/cli/gateway-cli/run-loop.ts`: Added `serverStarting` boolean guard to ignore spurious `SIGTERM` signals only while the server is actively initializing.\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary)**: The core WebSocket connection logic, the RPC protocol, and the graceful shutdown sequence for intentional stops remain completely untouched. This fix only affects systemd signal routing and adds a defensive check during the millisecond-level server initialization window.\\n\\n### Reproduction\\n1. Run Gateway as a systemd user service with `Restart=always`.\\n2. Run any CLI command: `openclaw cron list`.\\n3. Observe Gateway receives `SIGTERM` immediately after CLI exits.\\n4. With this PR, the Gateway will no longer receive `SIGTERM` from the CLI exit, and even if a spurious signal arrives during the restart loop, the `serverStarting` guard will break the loop.\\n\\n### Risk / Mitigation\\n- **Risk**: Changing `KillMode` to `mixed` might leave orphaned child processes (like ACP workers) running if they don\\u0026#39;t respond to `SIGKILL`. Ignoring `SIGTERM` during the `serverStarting` window might theoretically delay an intentional `systemctl stop` command if issued at the exact millisecond of startup.\\n- **Mitigation**: Systemd\\u0026#39;s `mixed` mode guarantees that `SIGKILL` is sent to all remaining processes in the cgroup after `TimeoutStopSec` (30s), so orphaned processes are still cleaned up reliably. The `serverStarting` guard window is extremely narrow (only during `params.start()`), meaning an intentional stop will either arrive before start, or immediately after, guaranteeing a graceful shutdown.\\n\\n### Change Type (select all)\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n\\n### Scope (select all touched areas)\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n\\n### Linked Issue/PR\\nFixes #47133\\nRelated to #29827, #27590\\n\\n### AI-Assisted Contribution\\n- **AI Usage**: This PR was developed with AI assistance.\\n- **Human Review**: I have personally reviewed, designed, and fully understand all the code changes.\\n- **Testing**: Fully tested locally with my OpenClaw instance.\\n\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/47222\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"openperf\",\"id\":80630709,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/openperf\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/80630709?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"gateway\",\"cli\",\"size: XS\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"fix-gateway-sigterm-restart\",\"sha\":\"574f49e2c257a6e0a0d29a1872f288a2f7d2214b\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"openperf/moltbot\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant. This happens with zero debug logs and leaves the user with a dead gateway.\\n- **Root Cause**: In `src/browser/chrome-mcp.ts`, `createRealSession()` initializes a `ready` promise as an IIFE that immediately starts the MCP handshake (`client.connect()`). However, this promise lacked a synchronous `.catch()` handler. If the subprocess failed quickly, the promise rejected *before* `getSession()` had a chance to `await session.ready`. This resulted in an Unhandled Promise Rejection, which triggered the gateway\\u0026#39;s fatal error handler (`process.exit(1)`). Additionally, the subprocess `stderr` pipe was never consumed (losing diagnostic info), and the handshake had no timeout.\\n- **Fix**: \\n  1. Attached a no-op `.catch(() =\\u0026gt; {})` immediately to the `ready` promise to prevent the unhandled rejection (the actual error is still properly thrown and handled when `getSession()` awaits it).\\n  2. Implemented a `drainStderr` utility to consume the subprocess `stderr` stream into a bounded buffer, preventing back-pressure deadlocks and capturing error output for the exception message.\\n  3. Added a `Promise.race` with a 30-second timeout to the handshake to prevent the gateway from hanging indefinitely if the subprocess stalls.\\n- **What changed**: \\n  - `src/browser/chrome-mcp.ts`: Added `drainStderr` function, added timeout to the `ready` handshake, appended stderr to the `BrowserProfileUnavailableError` message, and added the crucial `.catch()` to the `ready` promise.\\n- **What did NOT change (scope boundary)**: \\n  - Did not change the MCP SDK transport implementation.\\n  - Did not change how other browser profiles (e.g., standard CDP) connect or operate.\\n  - Did not change the `chrome-devtools-mcp` spawning arguments.\\n\\n### Reproduction\\n1. Configure a browser profile with `driver: \\u0026#34;existing-session\\u0026#34;`.\\n2. Ensure no Chrome instance is running on the expected port (or block the port).\\n3. Attempt to use the profile.\\n4. **Before**: The gateway process crashes completely due to an unhandled rejection.\\n5. **After**: The gateway gracefully catches the failure, logs the subprocess stderr, and throws a standard `BrowserProfileUnavailableError` without crashing.\\n\\n### Risk / Mitigation\\n- **Risk**: The stderr buffer could consume too much memory if the subprocess spams logs.\\n- **Mitigation**: Implemented a bounded buffer (`maxBytes = 8192`) in `drainStderr` that drops older chunks when the limit is exceeded, ensuring memory safety.\\n\\n### Change Type (select all)\\n- [x] Bug fix\\n\\n### Scope (select all touched areas)\\n- [x] Gateway / orchestration\\n\\n### Linked Issue/PR\\nFixes #47965\\n\\n### AI-Assisted Contribution\\n- **AI Usage**: This PR was developed with AI assistance.\\n- **Human Review**: I have personally reviewed, designed, and fully understand all the code changes.\\n- **Testing**: Fully tested locally with my OpenClaw instance (all 428 browser tests passed).\",\"state\":\"open\",\"draft\":false,\"merged\":false,\"html_url\":\"https://github.com/openclaw/openclaw/pull/48001\",\"user\":{\"login\":\"openperf\",\"id\":80630709,\"profile_url\":\"https://github.com/openperf\",\"avatar_url\":\"https://avatars.githubusercontent.com/u/80630709?v=4\"},\"labels\":[\"size: S\"],\"head\":{\"ref\":\"fix/issue-47965-mcp-handshake-crash\",\"sha\":\"5b5a48b2e9aab81267879d4b4068c9d6be5c980d\",\"repo\":{\"full_name\":\"openperf/moltbot\",\"description\":\"Your own personal AI assistant.
